2:23:1294:0:14:72:473:700:12:Times:12:g_d0_f1:C:The Macroeconomic Impact of Microeconomic Shocks: Beyond Hulten's Theorem 
2:24:1367:14:14:72:276:686:12:Times:12:Times:C:David Rezza Baqaee and Emmanuel Farhi
2:25:1404:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:C:NBER Working Paper No. 23145
2:26:1432:14:14:72:266:658:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:February 2017, Revised December 2018
2:27:1468:14:28:72:218:644:12:Times:12:Times:C:JEL No. E01,E1,E23,E32,L16
2:28:1494:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:C:ABSTRACT
2:29:1502:28:14:72:546:588:12:Times:12:Times:C:We  provide  a  nonlinear  characterization  of  the  macroeconomic  impact  of  microeconomic 
2:30:1597:14:14:72:546:574:12:Times:12:Times:C:productivity shocks in terms of reduced-form non-parametric elasticities for efficient economies. 
2:31:1694:14:14:72:545:560:12:Times:12:Times:C:We  also  show how  structural  microeconomic  parameters  are  mapped  to  these  reduced-form 
2:32:1789:14:14:72:545:546:12:Times:12:Times:C:general  equilibrium  elasticities. In  this  sense,  we  extend  the  foundational  theorem  of  Hulten 
2:33:1893:14:14:72:546:532:12:Times:12:Times:C:(1978)  beyond  first-order  terms  to  capture nonlinearities.  Key  features  ignored  by  first-order 
2:34:1997:14:14:72:545:518:12:Times:12:Times:C:approximations  that  play  a  crucial  role  are:  structural elasticities  of  substitution,  network 
2:35:2100:14:14:72:546:504:12:Times:12:Times:C:linkages,  structural  returns  to  scale,  and  the  extent  of  factor  reallocation. In  a  business-cycle 
2:36:2209:14:14:72:545:490:12:Times:12:Times:C:calibration  with  sectoral  shocks,  nonlinearities  magnify  negative  shocks  and  attenuate positive 
2:37:2313:14:14:72:543:476:12:Times:12:Times:C:shocks, resulting in an aggregate output distribution that is asymmetric (negative skewness), fat-
2:38:2410:14:14:72:545:462:12:Times:12:g_d0_f2:C:tailed (excess kurtosis), and has a lower mean, even when shocks are symmetric and thin-tailed. 
2:39:2505:14:14:72:546:448:12:Times:12:Times:C:Average output losses due to short-run sectoral shocks are an order of magnitude larger than the 
2:40:2602:14:14:72:545:434:12:Times:12:Times:C:welfare cost of business cycles calculated by Lucas (1987). Nonlinearities can also cause shocks 
2:41:2698:14:14:72:545:420:12:Times:12:Times:C:to  critical sectors  to  have  disproportionate  macroeconomic  effects,  almost  tripling  the  estimated 
2:42:2805:14:14:72:546:406:12:Times:12:Times:C:impact of the 1970s oil shocks on world aggregate output. Finally, in a long-run growth context, 
2:43:2901:14:14:72:545:392:12:Times:12:Times:C:nonlinearities,  which underpin  Baumol’s  cost  disease  via  the  increase  over  time  in  the  sales 
2:44:3005:14:14:72:545:378:12:Times:12:Times:C:shares of low-growth bottleneck sectors, account for a 20 percentage point reduction in aggregate 
2:45:3102:14:42:72:311:364:12:Times:12:Times:C:TFP growth over the period 1948-2014 in the US.
2:46:3148:42:14:72:172:322:12:Times:12:Times:C:David Rezza Baqaee
2:47:3166:14:14:72:105:308:12:Times:12:Times:C:UCLA
2:48:3170:14:14:72:157:294:12:Times:12:Times:C:315 Portola Plaza
2:49:3187:14:14:72:132:280:12:Times:12:Times:C:Los Angeles
2:50:3198:14:28:72:183:266:12:Times:12:Times:C:D.R.Baqaee@lse.ac.uk
2:51:3218:28:14:72:152:238:12:Times:12:Times:C:Emmanuel Farhi
2:52:3232:14:14:72:165:224:12:Times:12:Times:C:Harvard University
2:53:3250:14:14:72:198:210:12:Times:12:Times:C:Department of Economics
2:54:3273:14:14:72:145:196:12:Times:12:Times:C:Littauer Center
2:55:3288:14:14:72:184:182:12:Times:12:Times:C:Cambridge, MA 02138
2:56:3307:14:14:72:124:168:12:Times:12:Times:C:and NBER
2:57:3315:14:0:72:210:154:12:Times:12:Times:C:emmanuel.farhi@gmail.com
3:58:3339:0:31:72:197:707:17:g_d0_f4:17:g_d0_f4:C:1    Introduction
3:59:3356:31:18:72:540:676:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:The foundational theorem of Hulten (1978) states that for efficient economies and under
3:60:3443:18:18:72:540:658:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:minimal  assumptions,  the  impact  on  aggregate  TFP  of  a  microeconomic  TFP  shock  is
3:61:3535:18:32:72:369:640:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:equal to the shocked producer’s sales as a share of GDP:
3:62:3591:32:0:238:299:608:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f6:A:d logTFP=
3:63:3600:0:26:302:319:620:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:C:∑
3:64:3601:26:0:309:311:594:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:F:i
3:65:3602:0:40:321:375:608:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:C:λid logAi,
3:66:3612:40:18:72:491:568:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:where d logAiis a shock to produceriandλiis its sales share or Domar weight.
3:67:3688:18:18:89:539:550:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Hulten’s theorem is a cornerstone result in productivity and growth accounting:  it
3:68:3771:18:18:71:539:532:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:shows  how  to  construct  aggregate  TFP  growth  from  microeconomic  TFP  growth,  and
3:69:3860:18:18:71:539:514:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:provides structurally-interpretable decompositions of changes of national or sectoral ag-
3:70:3949:18:18:71:539:496:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:gregates into the changes of their disaggregated component industries or firms.  It also
3:71:4037:18:18:71:539:478:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:provides the benchmark answers for counterfactual questions in structural models with
3:72:4122:18:18:71:211:460:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:disaggregated production.
3:73:4147:18:18:89:539:442:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:The surprising generality of the result has led economists to de-emphasize the role of
3:74:4233:18:17:71:539:424:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:microeconomic and network production structures in macroeconomic models. After all, if
3:75:4319:17:18:71:539:407:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:sales summarize the macroeconomic impact of microeconomic shocks and we can directly
3:76:4403:18:18:71:539:389:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:observe  sales,  then  we  need  not  concern  ourselves  with  the  details  of  the  underlying
3:77:4500:18:18:71:539:371:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:disaggregated system that gave rise to these sales.  Since it seems to imply that the very
3:78:4590:18:18:71:539:353:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:object of its study is irrelevant for macroeconomics, Hulten’s theorem has been something
3:79:4679:18:18:71:424:335:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:of a bugbear for the burgeoning literature on production networks.
3:80:4745:18:18:89:539:317:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Are these conclusions warranted?  Even at a purely intuitive level, there are reasons
3:81:4830:18:18:71:539:299:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:to  be  skeptical.   For  example,  thinking  through  the  lens  of  Hulten’s  theorem  leads  to
3:82:4928:18:18:71:539:281:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the questionable prediction that negative shocks to Walmart and to electricity production,
3:83:5018:18:18:71:539:263:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:which both have a Domar weight of around 4%, should have the same impact on aggregate
3:84:5103:18:18:71:110:245:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:output.
3:85:5110:18:18:89:539:227:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:In  this  paper,  we  challenge  the  view  that  the  macroeconomic  importance  of  a  mi-
3:86:5202:18:18:71:539:209:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:croeconomic  sector  is  summarized  by  its  sales  and,  more  broadly,  the  notion  that  the
3:87:5299:18:18:71:539:191:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:microeconomic  details  of  the  production  structure  are  irrelevant  for  macroeconomics.
3:88:5392:18:17:71:539:173:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:They key is to recognize that Hulten’s theorem only provides a first-order approxima-
3:89:5477:17:18:71:539:156:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:tion. Nonlinearities can significantly degrade the quality of the first-order approximation
3:90:5568:18:18:71:539:138:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:for large enough shocks.  To capture these nonlinearities, we provide a general second-
3:91:5655:18:18:71:539:120:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:order approximation by characterizing the derivatives of Domar weights with respect to
3:92:5741:18:18:71:539:102:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:shocks. The second-order terms are shaped by the microeconomic details of the disaggre-
3:93:5828:18:0:71:539:84:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:gated production structure:  network linkages, microeconomic elasticities of substitution
4:94:5918:0:18:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:in production,  microeconomic returns to scale,  and the degree to which factors can be
4:95:6005:18:18:72:133:690:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:reallocated.
4:96:6017:18:18:89:539:672:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Our results are general in that they apply to any efficient general equilibrium economy.
4:97:6105:18:18:72:540:654:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:They  suggest  that  Cobb-Douglas  models,  commonly  used  in  the  production-network,
4:98:6193:18:18:72:540:636:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:growth, and multi-sector macroeconomics literatures, are very special: the Domar weights
4:99:6281:18:18:72:540:618:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:are constant, the first-order approximation is exact, the model is log-linear, and as a result,
4:100:6376:18:18:72:540:600:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the microeconomic details of the production structure are irrelevant.1These knife-edge
4:101:6462:18:18:72:418:582:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:properties disappear as soon as one deviates from Cobb-Douglas.
4:102:6525:18:18:89:539:564:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:We  also  show  that  nonlinearities  in  production  matter  quantitatively  for  a  number
4:103:6617:18:18:72:539:546:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:of macroeconomic phenomena operating at different frequencies, ranging from the role
4:104:6701:18:18:72:540:528:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:of sectoral shocks in business cycles to the impact of oil shocks and the importance of
4:105:6788:18:25:72:299:510:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Baumol’s cost disease for long-run growth:
4:106:6830:25:18:86:540:485:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:1.  Using a calibrated structural multi-industry model with realistic complementarities
4:107:6917:18:18:101:540:467:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:in production, we find that nonlinearities amplify the impact of negative sectoral
4:108:6999:18:18:101:540:449:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:shocks and mitigate the impact of positive sectoral shocks.2,3Large negative shocks
4:109:7082:18:18:101:539:431:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:to crucial industries, like “oil and gas”, have a significantly larger negative effect on
4:110:7171:18:18:101:540:413:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:aggregate output than negative shocks to larger but less crucial industries such as
4:111:7254:18:18:101:540:395:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:“retail trade”.  Nonlinearities also have a significant impact on the distribution of
4:112:7339:18:17:101:540:377:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:aggregate output:  they lower its mean and generate negative skewness and excess
4:113:7419:17:18:101:540:360:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:kurtosis even though the underlying shocks are symmetric and thin tailed.  Non-
4:114:7498:18:18:101:540:342:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:linearities in production generate significant welfare costs of sectoral fluctuations,
4:115:7584:18:18:101:540:324:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:ranging from 0.2% to 1.3% depending on the calibration. These are an order of mag-
4:116:7666:18:18:101:540:306:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:nitude larger than the welfare costs of business cycles arising from nonlinearities in
4:117:7752:18:27:101:354:288:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:utility (risk aversion) identified by Lucas (1987).
4:118:7803:27:18:86:540:261:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:2.  We derive and use a simple nonparametric formula, taking into account the observed
4:119:7889:18:16:85:539:243:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:1A mixture of analytical tractability, as well as balanced-growth considerations, have made Cobb-Douglas
4:120:7993:16:12:72:539:227:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f5:F:thecanonical production function for networks (Long and Plosser, 1983), multisector RBC models (Gomme
4:121:8094:12:12:72:540:215:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:and Rupert, 2007), and growth theory (Aghion and Howitt, 2008).  Recent work by Grossman et al. (2016)
4:122:8196:12:8:72:349:203:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:shows how balanced growth can occur without Cobb-Douglas.
4:123:8253:8:16:85:539:195:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:2The empirical literature on production networks, like Atalay (2017), Boehm et al. (2017), and Barrot and
4:124:8358:16:12:72:540:179:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:Sauvagnat (2016) all find that structural elasticities of substitution in production are significantly below one,
4:125:8471:12:12:72:540:167:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:and sometimes very close to zero, across intermediate inputs, and between intermediate inputs and labor at
4:126:8577:12:12:72:540:155:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:business cycle frequencies. Furthermore, a voluminous literature on structural transformation, building on
4:127:8683:12:12:72:540:143:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:Baumol (1967), has found evidence in favor of non-unitary elasticities of substitution in consumption and
4:128:8788:12:8:72:266:131:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:production across sectors over the long-run.
4:129:8832:8:16:85:539:123:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:3While complementarities prevail at the sectoral level,  substituabilities dominate across firms within
4:130:8935:16:12:72:540:107:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:sectors. This implies that while nonlinearities tend to amplify negative sectoral-level shocks and to attenuate
4:131:9046:12:12:72:540:95:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:positive sectoral-level shocks, they tend to attenuate negative firm-level shocks and to amplify positive firm-
4:132:9157:12:12:72:539:83:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:level shocks.  Nonlinearities therefore introduce an important qualitative difference between sectoral- and
4:133:9264:12:0:72:360:71:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:firm-level shocks which is absent from the linearized perspective.
5:134:9331:0:18:101:540:708:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:change in the Domar weight for crude oil, to analyze the impact of the energy crisis
5:135:9415:18:18:101:540:690:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:of the 1970s up to the second order.  We find that nonlinearities almost tripled the
5:136:9499:18:28:101:480:672:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:impact of the oil shocks from 0.23% to 0.61% of world aggregate output.
5:137:9570:28:18:86:540:644:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:3.  We show that the nonlinearities are also important for long-run growth in the pres-
5:138:9657:18:18:101:540:626:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:ence of realistic complementarities across sectors. They cause the Domar weights of
5:139:9740:18:18:101:540:608:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:bottleneck sectors with relatively low productivity growth to grow over time and
5:140:9820:18:18:101:539:590:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:thereby reduce aggregate growth, an effect identified as Baumol’s cost disease (Bau-
5:141:9904:18:18:101:540:572:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:mol, 1967).  We calculate that nonlinearities have reduced the growth of aggregate
5:142:9986:18:28:101:447:554:12:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f5:A:TFP by 20 percentage points over the period 1948-2014 in the US.4
5:143:10051:28:18:89:539:526:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:The  outline  of  the  paper  is  as  follows.   In  Section  2,  we  derive  a  general  formula
5:144:10148:18:18:71:539:508:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:describing  the  second-order  impact  on  aggregate  output  of  shocks  in  terms  of  non-
5:145:10241:18:18:71:540:490:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:parametric  sufficient  statistics:  reduced-form  general-equilibrium  elasticities  of  substi-
5:146:10338:18:17:71:539:472:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:tution and input-output multipliers.5We explain the implications of this formula for the
5:147:10426:17:18:71:539:455:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:impact of correlated shocks and for the average performance of the economy.  In Section
5:148:10513:18:18:71:539:437:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:3, we use two special illustrative examples to provide some intuition for the roles of the
5:149:10603:18:18:71:539:419:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:general-equilibrium elasticities of substitution and of the input-output multipliers and for
5:150:10695:18:18:71:539:401:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:their dependence on microeconomic primitives. In Section 4, we fully characterize second-
5:151:10784:18:18:71:539:383:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:order terms in terms of microeconomic primitives for general nested-CES economies with
5:152:10870:18:18:71:539:365:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:arbitrary microeconomic elasticities of substitution and network linkages.  In Section 5,
5:153:10959:18:18:71:539:347:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:we further generalize the results to arbitrary (potentially non-CES) production functions.
5:154:11049:18:36:71:539:329:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:In Section 6, we provide some illustrations of the quantitative implications of our results.
5:155:11141:36:18:71:539:293:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f5:B:Related literature.Gabaix (2011) and Acemoglu et al. (2012) revived interest in Hulten’s
5:156:11229:18:18:71:539:275:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:theorem in the context of short-run aggregate fluctuations.  Gabaix (2011) uses Hulten’s
5:157:11317:18:18:71:540:257:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:theorem to argue that the existence of very large, or in his languagegranularfirms, can
5:158:11404:18:19:71:539:239:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:be a possible source of aggregate volatility.  If there exist very large firms, then shocks to
5:159:11498:19:15:85:539:220:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:4The literature on structural transformation emphasizes two key forces: non-unitary elasticities of substi-
5:160:11605:15:12:72:540:205:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:tution and non-homotheticities.  Both forces cause sales shares to change in response to exogenous shocks.
5:161:11711:12:12:72:540:193:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:Since  Hulten’s  theorem  implies  that  sales  shares  are  equal  to  derivatives  of  the  aggregate  output  func-
5:162:11829:12:12:72:540:181:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:tion, anything that causes the derivative to change is a non-linearity.  By characterizing the second-order
5:163:11936:12:12:72:540:169:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:terms in a general way, our results encompass both non-unitary elasticities and non-homotheticities.   In
5:164:12041:12:12:72:539:157:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:fact, non-homotheticities canalwaysbe turned into non-unitary elasticities of substitution by adding more
5:165:12146:12:9:72:195:145:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:fixed-factors to an economy.
5:166:12174:9:15:85:539:136:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:5Studying the second-order terms is the first step in grappling with the nonlinearities inherent in mutli-
5:167:12280:15:12:72:540:121:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:sector models with production networks. In this sense, our work illustrates the macroeconomic importance
5:168:12384:12:12:72:539:109:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:oflocaland  stronglynonlinearinteractions  emphasized  in  reduced  form  by  Scheinkman  and  Woodford
5:169:12487:12:12:72:540:97:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:(1994).   Other related work on nonlinear propagation of shocks in economic networks includes Durlauf
5:170:12588:12:12:72:540:85:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:(1993), Jovanovic (1987), Ballester et al. (2006) Acemoglu et al. (2015), Elliott et al. (2014), and especially
5:171:12699:12:0:72:173:73:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:Acemoglu et al. (2016).
6:172:12723:0:18:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:those firms will not cancel out with shocks to much smaller firms, resulting in aggregate
6:173:12812:18:18:72:540:690:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:fluctuations.  Acemoglu et al. (2012), working with a Cobb-Douglas model in the spirit
6:174:12898:18:18:72:540:672:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:of Long and Plosser (1983), observed that in an economy with input-output linkages, the
6:175:12985:18:18:72:540:654:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:equilibrium size of firms will depend on the shape of the input-output matrix.  Central
6:176:13072:18:18:72:540:636:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:suppliers will be weighted more highly than peripheral firms, and therefore, shocks to
6:177:13158:18:18:72:539:618:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:those central players will not cancel out with shocks to small firms.6Carvalho and Gabaix
6:178:13247:18:18:72:540:600:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:(2013)  show  how  Hulten’s  theorem  can  be  operationalized  to  decompose  the  sectoral
6:179:13339:18:18:72:235:582:12:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f5:B:sources of aggregate volatility.7
6:180:13372:18:18:89:539:564:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Relatedly, Acemoglu et al. (2017) deploy Hulten’s theorem to study other moments of
6:181:13455:18:18:72:540:546:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the distribution of aggregate output.  They argue that if the Domar weights are fat-tailed
6:182:13545:18:18:72:540:528:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:and if the underlying idiosyncratic shocks are fat-tailed, then aggregate output can exhibit
6:183:13637:18:18:72:539:510:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:non-normal behavior.  Stated differently, they show that aggregate output can inherit tail
6:184:13727:18:18:72:540:492:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:risk  from  idiosyncratic  tail  risk  if  the  distribution  of  the  Domar  weights  is  fat-tailed.
6:185:13829:18:17:72:540:474:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Our paper strengthens, but is distinct from, this point.  We find that, for the empirically
6:186:13920:17:18:72:540:457:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:relevant range of parameters, the response of aggregate output to shocks is significantly
6:187:14009:18:18:72:540:439:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:asymmetric.   Therefore,  the nonlinearity inherent in the production structure can turn
6:188:14097:18:18:72:540:421:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:even symmetric thin-tailed sectoral shocks into rare disasters endogenously.  This means
6:189:14185:18:18:72:540:403:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:that the economy could plausibly experience aggregate tail risk without either fat-tailed
6:190:14274:18:18:72:260:385:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:shocks or fat-tailed Domar weights.
6:191:14309:18:18:89:539:367:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:In a recent survey article Gabaix (2016), invoking Hulten’s theorem, writes “networks
6:192:14394:18:18:72:540:349:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:are a particular case of granularity rather than an alternative to it.” This has meant that re-
6:193:14489:18:18:72:539:331:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:searchers studying the role of networks have either moved away from efficient models, or
6:194:14577:18:18:72:540:313:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:that they have retreated from studying aggregate output and turned their attention to the
6:195:14666:18:18:72:540:295:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:microeconomic implications of networks, namely the covariance of fluctuations between
6:196:14751:18:17:72:539:277:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:different industries and firms.8,9However, models with the same sales distributions are
6:197:14838:17:16:85:539:260:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:6A  related  version  of  this  argument  was  also  advanced  by  Horvath  (1998),  who  explored  this  issue
6:198:14949:16:12:72:540:244:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:quantitatively with a more general model in Horvath (2000). Separately, Carvalho (2010) also explores how
6:199:15054:12:8:72:454:232:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:the law of large numbers may fail under certain conditions on the input-output matrix.
6:200:15140:8:16:85:539:224:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:7Results  related  to  Hulten’s  theorem  are  also  used  in  international  trade,  e.g.   Burstein  and  Cravino
6:201:15255:16:8:72:318:208:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:(2015), to infer the global gains from international trade.
6:202:15314:8:16:85:539:200:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:8Some  recent  papers  have  investigated  aggregate  volatility  in  production  networks  with  inefficient
6:203:15423:16:11:72:540:184:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:equilibria (where Hulten’s theorem does not hold).  Some examples include Bigio and La’O (2016), Baqaee
6:204:15526:11:12:72:540:173:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:(2016), Altinoglu (2016), Grassi (2017), and Baqaee and Farhi (2017).   See also Jones (2011), Jones (2013),
6:205:15634:12:9:72:302:161:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:Bartelme and Gorodnichenko (2015), and Liu (2017).
6:206:15684:9:15:85:539:152:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:9For instance, Foerster et al. (2011), Atalay (2017), Di Giovanni et al. (2014), and Stella (2015) investigate the
6:207:15798:15:12:72:540:137:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:importance of idiosyncratic shocks propagating through networks to generate cross-sectional covariances,
6:208:15902:12:12:72:540:125:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:but they refrain from analyzing the impact of these shocks on aggregate output. Atalay (2017) is particularly
6:209:16011:12:12:72:540:113:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:relevant in this context, since he finds that structural elasticities of substitution in production play a powerful
6:210:16126:12:12:72:540:101:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:role in generating covariance in sectoral output.  Our paper complements this analysis by focusing instead
6:211:16232:12:0:72:311:89:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:on the way complementarities affect aggregate output.
7:212:16286:0:18:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:only equivalent up to the first-order, and in this paper, we highlight the fragility of this
7:213:16378:18:47:72:210:690:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:first-order approximation.

7:256:17532:18:18:89:540:116:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:We interpretYas a cardinal measure of (real) aggregate output and note that it is the
7:257:17617:18:18:71:539:98:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:correct measure of the household’s “standard of living” in this model. We implicitly rely
7:258:17706:18:0:71:539:80:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:on the existence of complete financial markets and homotheticity of preferences to ensure
8:259:17796:0:18:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the existence of a representative consumer.  Although the assumption of a representative
8:260:17884:18:18:72:540:690:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:consumer is not strictly necessary for the results in this section, it is a standard assumption
8:261:17979:18:18:72:540:672:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:in this literature since it allows us to unambiguously define and measure changes in real
8:262:18068:18:18:72:510:654:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:aggregate output without contending with the issue of the appropriate price index.
8:263:18150:18:18:89:540:636:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:We  assume  that  the  production  functionFiof  each  goodihas  constant  returns  to
8:264:18236:18:18:72:540:618:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:scale, which implies that equilibrium profits are zero.  This is without loss of generality
8:265:18327:18:18:72:540:600:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:because  decreasing  returns  to  scale  can  be  captured  by  adding  fixed  factors  to  which
8:266:18424:18:18:72:540:582:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the corresponding profits accrue.  The assumption that shocks are Hicks-neutral is also
8:267:18511:18:18:72:540:564:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:without  loss  of  generality:   we  can  represent  an  input-specific  productivity  shock  by
8:268:18607:18:18:72:540:546:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:adding a new producer that produces that input and hitting this new producer with a
8:269:18690:18:18:72:539:528:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Hicks-neutral shock.10Finally, note that goods could represent different varieties of goods
8:270:18781:18:18:72:540:510:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:from the same industry, goods from different industries, or even goods in different time
8:271:18869:18:18:72:268:492:12:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f5:B:periods, regions, or states of nature.11
8:272:18909:18:17:89:539:474:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:DefineY(A1,...,AN) to be the equilibrium aggregate output as a function of the exoge-

15:736:36046:40:26:71:285:507:14:g_d0_f4:14:g_d0_f4:C:Welfare Costs of Sectoral Shocks
15:737:36078:26:18:71:539:481:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:For the majority of the paper, we focus on log aggregate output, which can be characterized
15:738:36169:18:18:71:539:463:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:with unit-less elasticities.   With complementarities,  we have argued that sector shocks
15:739:36258:18:18:71:539:445:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:lower the mean of log aggregate output, an effect which we can interpret as the welfare
15:740:36345:18:18:71:539:427:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:cost of sectoral shocks. One may imagine that the losses from uncertainty that we identify
15:741:36435:18:18:71:539:409:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:depend on the concavity of the log function. A consumer with log utility prefers a mean-
15:742:36523:18:18:71:539:391:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:preserving reduction in uncertainty even when the aggregate output function is linear.
15:743:36609:18:18:71:539:373:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:However,  as  shown  by  Lucas  (1987),  the  corresponding  losses  are  extremely  small  in
15:744:36703:18:18:71:539:355:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:practice in business-cycle settings.  The much larger effects that we identify originate in
15:745:36794:18:18:71:539:337:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:nonlinearities in production, and they are present even when the utility function is linear
15:746:36885:18:18:71:212:319:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:in aggregate consumption.
15:747:36910:18:18:89:539:301:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:The  following  proposition  formalizes  this  intuition  and  shows  that  the  Lucas-style
15:748:37002:18:18:71:539:283:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:welfare losses due to nonlinearities in the utility function in the form of risk-aversion and
15:749:37095:18:18:71:539:265:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the losses due to nonlinearities in production do not interact with one-another up to a
15:750:37182:18:27:71:234:247:12:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f5:B:second-order approximation.20

16:782:37860:28:18:89:539:680:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:The first term on the right-hand side, which is quantitatively small, is the traditional
16:783:37948:18:18:71:539:662:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Lucas-style cost arising from curvature in the utility function.  The second term, which is

16:785:38127:18:41:71:300:626:12:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f5:B:on the coefficient of relative risk aversion.21
16:786:38174:41:26:71:273:585:14:g_d0_f4:14:g_d0_f4:C:Mapping From Micro to Macro
16:787:38201:26:18:71:539:559:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Theorem 2 implies that the GE elasticities of substitutionρi jand the elasticity of the input-
16:788:38295:18:18:71:539:541:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:output multiplier d logξ/d logAiare sufficient statistics for the second-order impact of
16:789:38383:18:18:71:539:523:12:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f7:B:shocks.   However,  these sufficient statistics are reduced-form elasticities,  and unlikeλi
16:790:38475:18:18:71:540:505:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:andξ, they are not readily observable.  Furthermore, since they are general equilibrium
16:791:38562:18:18:71:539:487:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:objects, they cannot be identified through exogenous microeconomic variation. So, while
16:792:38649:18:18:71:539:469:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:careful empirical work can identify micro-elasticities,  the leap from micro-estimates to
16:793:38738:18:17:71:239:451:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:macro-effects can be hazardous.
16:794:38769:17:18:89:539:434:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:In this paper, we provide the mapping from structural micro parameters to the reduced-
16:795:38855:18:18:71:539:416:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:form  GE  elasticities.   This  general  characterization  can  be  found  in  Section  4  for  CES
16:796:38954:18:18:71:539:398:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:networks,  and in Section 5 for arbitrary networks.   However,  rather than stating these
16:797:39043:18:18:71:539:380:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:results up front, we build up to the general characterization using some important special
16:798:39133:18:47:71:165:362:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:cases in Section 3.
16:799:39152:47:31:71:264:315:17:g_d0_f4:17:g_d0_f4:C:3    Illustrative Examples
16:800:39178:31:18:71:539:284:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:In this section, we work through two special cases to illustrate and isolate some intuition
16:801:39269:18:18:71:540:266:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:for how the GE elasticities of substitution and the input-output multiplier affect the shape
16:802:39361:18:18:71:539:248:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:of the aggregate output function.  After working through these examples, we provide a
16:803:39446:18:40:71:435:230:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:generic characterization of the second-order terms in Section 4 and 5.

19:1006:44457:36:18:71:539:388:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:one in the opposite direction,  and so the relative shareλi/λjremains constant.   When

19:1011:44886:18:17:89:539:298:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Let us consider the Leontief limitθ0→0.  In this limit, the first-order term becomes

19:1013:45055:18:18:72:540:263:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:treme. Following a negative shock toi, the relative pricepi/pjjumps to infinity, and so does
19:1014:45147:18:18:72:540:245:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the relative shareλi/λj.  Following a positive shock, the relative price jumps to zero and
19:1015:45237:18:18:72:540:227:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:so does the relative share. The associated amplification of negative shocks and mitigation
19:1016:45327:18:18:72:229:209:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:of negative shocks is extreme.
19:1017:45357:18:18:89:540:191:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Let us now consider the perfect-substitutes limitθ0→∞. Positive shocks are amplified
19:1018:45441:18:18:71:539:173:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:and negative shocks are mitigated, but the effect is not nearly so dramatic. In fact, because

19:1020:45625:18:18:71:540:137:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:shareλi/λjmoves one-for-one with the shock toi.  The situation is depicted graphically

20:1057:46958:36:18:89:539:378:12:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f7:A:Because labor can be costlessly reallocated across producers,  the relative pricepi/pj

20:1063:47478:18:18:72:539:270:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:increases when it is positive. Whenθ0>1, relative quantity moves more than one-for-one
20:1064:47564:18:18:72:539:252:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:with the shock as labor is reallocated away fromiwhen the shock is negative and towards
20:1065:47651:18:18:72:539:234:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f5:B:iwhen it is positive.  As a result, the relative share decreases when the shock is negative,
20:1066:47743:18:18:72:246:216:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:and increases when it is positive.
20:1067:47777:18:17:89:540:198:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f7:A:Contrary to what one may have assumed, a near-Leontief production function isnot
20:1068:47857:17:18:72:540:181:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:sufficient for generating large deviations from Hulten’s theorem, as long as factors can
20:1069:47945:18:18:72:540:163:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:be reallocated freely, precisely because this reallocation is successful at reinforcing “weak
20:1070:48038:18:18:72:540:145:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:links”. In the Leontief limit, the relative quantityyi/yjis invariant to the shock, and so the
20:1071:48132:18:18:72:540:127:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:relative sales shareλi/λjmoves inversely one-for-one with the shock toi.  Relative to the
20:1072:48221:18:18:72:540:109:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:first-order approximation, the second-order approximation still amplifies negative shocks
20:1073:48310:18:18:72:540:91:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:and mitigates positive shocks, but the corresponding magnitudes are much smaller than
20:1074:48395:18:0:72:331:73:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:in the case where labor cannot not be reallocated.
21:1075:48447:0:18:89:539:708:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:In the perfect substitutes limit, labor is entirely allocated to the most productive pro-
21:1076:48536:18:18:72:539:690:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:ducer.  In response to a positive shock toi, the relative quantityyi/yjjumps to infinity,
21:1077:48625:18:18:71:540:672:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:and so does the relative shareλi/λj. In response to a negative shock, the relative quantity
21:1078:48716:18:18:71:539:654:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:drops to zero, and so does the relative share.  Relative to the first-order approximation,
21:1079:48806:18:18:71:539:636:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the  second-order  approximation  still  amplifies  positive  shocks  and  mitigates  negative
21:1080:48900:18:18:71:539:618:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:shocks, but the corresponding magnitudes are now much larger than in the case where
21:1081:48983:18:18:71:503:600:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:labor cannot not be reallocated. The situation is depicted graphically in Figure 1b.
21:1082:49067:18:18:89:539:582:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Finally, note that both when labor can or cannot be reallocated, the second-order term
21:1083:49153:18:18:71:540:564:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:scales  inλi(1−λi)  as  a  function  of  the  sizeλiof  the  shocked  produceri.   Its  absolute
21:1084:49249:18:18:71:540:546:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:value is therefore hump-shaped inλi:  it goes zero whenλiis close to 0 or 1, and reaches
21:1085:49337:18:18:71:539:528:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:a maximum whenλiis intermediate at 1/2.   That the term is small whenλiis close to
21:1086:49419:18:18:71:540:510:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:0 is intuitive.  That it is small whenλiis close to 1 makes sense since the then economy
21:1087:49507:18:18:71:539:492:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:behaves much like produceriand aggregate output is then close to being proportional to
21:1088:49593:18:17:71:487:474:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f5:B:Ai. The second-order term can only be significant for intermediate values ofλi.
21:1089:49672:17:18:89:539:457:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:To recap, with complementarities: a negative shock can cause a large downturn when
21:1090:49754:18:18:71:539:439:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:labor cannot be freely re-allocated, but the ability to re-allocate labor largely mitigates these
21:1091:49851:18:18:71:539:421:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:effects; positive shocks have a lesser impact. By contrast, with substitutabilities: a positive
21:1092:49946:18:18:71:539:403:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:shock can cause a big boom when labor can be re-allocated, but the inability to re-allocated
21:1093:50038:18:18:71:539:385:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:labor mitigates these effects; negative shocks have a lesser impact.  Cobb-Douglas stands
21:1094:50127:18:18:71:539:367:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:as a special case where the macroeconomic impact of microeconomic shocks is symmetric
21:1095:50212:18:18:71:539:349:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:independently of whether or not labor can be reallocated (since the equilibrium allocation
21:1096:50302:18:18:71:540:331:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:of labor across producers is constant even when labor can be re-allocated).22These effects
21:1097:50392:18:18:71:539:313:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:are less pronounced when the size of the shocked producer is very small or very large,
21:1098:50478:18:40:71:336:295:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:and are more pronounced when it is intermediate.
21:1099:50526:40:27:71:265:255:14:g_d0_f4:14:g_d0_f4:C:3.2    Input-Output Multiplier
21:1100:50556:27:18:71:539:228:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:In the previous example of a horizontal economy, the input-output multiplierξis constant
21:1101:50644:18:17:71:539:210:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:and deviations from Hulten’s theorem are due to non-unitary GE elasticities of substitu-

22:1162:52348:19:16:82:539:112:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:23Proposition 6 shows that even though the gross production function is homogenous in productivity,
22:1163:52447:16:12:72:540:96:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:aggregate net output (value added) is not homogeneous of degree 1. Furthermore, aggregate output is not
22:1164:52550:12:0:72:431:84:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:homogenous of any degree in equilibrium, sinceξvaries in response to the shock.
23:1165:52631:0:18:89:540:708:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Intuitively, this results from the fact that output is used as its own input. Whenθ1=1,

23:1169:52983:18:18:72:448:636:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:larger is the steady-state input-output multiplier, the larger is the effect.

23:1187:53515:62:31:72:338:288:17:g_d0_f4:17:g_d0_f4:C:4    General nested-CES Networks
23:1188:53547:31:18:72:540:257:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:We now characterize the second-order terms for a general nested-CES economy (encom-
23:1189:53630:18:18:72:540:239:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:passing the examples in Section 3).  Any CES economy with a representative consumer,
23:1190:53714:18:18:72:540:221:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:an arbitrary numbers of nests, elasticities, and intermediate input use, can be re-written
23:1191:53804:18:17:72:539:203:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:in what we callstandard form, which is more convenient to study. Throughout this section,
23:1192:53893:17:20:72:534:186:12:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f5:B:variables with over-lines are normalizing constants equal to the values in steady-state.25
23:1193:53983:20:15:82:540:166:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:24Inthis  example,  whenθ1=0,  we  haveY=A/ω1l,  where  1/ω1lis  the  steady-state  input-output
23:1194:54079:15:12:72:540:151:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:multiplier.   Therefore,  although Hulten’s approximation fails in log terms,  Hulten’s theorem is globally
23:1195:54186:12:12:72:539:139:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:accurate inlinearterms.  This is a consequence of the fact that there is only one good.  In Appendix B, we
23:1196:54292:12:12:72:540:127:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:generalize this example to multiple goods, and show that output can be very strongly nonlinear even with
23:1197:54396:12:8:72:169:115:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:full labor reallocation.
23:1198:54420:8:16:82:539:107:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:25Since we are interested in log changes, the normalizing constants are irrelevant.  We use normalized
23:1199:54522:16:0:72:507:91:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:quantities since it simplifies calibration, and clarifies the fact that CES aggregators are not unit-less.
24:1200:54630:0:18:89:539:708:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:A CES economy in standard form is one where we treat each CES aggregator as a node
24:1201:54712:18:18:72:540:690:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:in  the  production  network,  with  an  accompanying  elasticity  of  substitution.   Through
24:1202:54806:18:18:72:540:672:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:a relabelling, this structure can represent any CES economy with an arbitrary pattern of
24:1203:54894:18:18:72:540:654:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:nests and elasticities. Intuitively, by relabelling each CES aggregator to be a new producer,
24:1204:54987:18:18:72:273:636:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:we can have as many nests as desired.
24:1205:55024:18:18:89:539:618:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:A CES economy in standard form is defined by a tuple (ω,θ,F) and a set of normalizing
24:1206:55109:18:18:72:540:600:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:constants (y,x). The (N+F+1)×(N+F+1) matrixωis a matrix of input-output parameters
24:1207:55191:18:18:72:540:582:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:where the first row and column correspond to household sector,  the nextNrows and
24:1208:55272:18:18:72:539:564:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:columns correspond to reproducible goods and the lastFrows and columns correspond
24:1209:55353:18:18:72:540:546:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:to factors. What distinguishes factors from goods is that factors cannot be produced. The
24:1210:55442:18:18:72:540:528:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:(N+1)×1 vectorθis a vector of microeconomic elasticities of substitution. For convenience
24:1211:55531:18:18:72:522:510:12:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f5:B:we use number indices starting at 0 instead of 1 to describe the elements ofωandθ.26
24:1212:55615:18:18:89:539:492:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:TheFfactors are modeled as non-reproducible goods and the production function of
24:1213:55695:18:10:71:224:474:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:these goods are endowments
24:1214:55721:10:18:289:298:464:12:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:C:yf

26:1328:57908:0:18:89:539:708:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Equations (10) and (11) have a simple intuition.  Let us focus first on equation (10).

26:1336:58551:18:18:72:539:564:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Leontief inverse.  Now consider a given producerk.  Ifθk<1, producerkincreases its

26:1338:58722:18:18:71:540:528:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:to the shock toj, as measured byΨ(j).  This increases the relative demand expenditure

26:1340:58893:18:18:71:539:492:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:of the Leontief inverseΨ(i).   The overall effect is stronger,  the higher is the covariance
26:1341:58985:18:17:71:540:474:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f5:B:CovΩ(k)(Ψ(i),Ψ(j)), the larger is the size of producerkas measured byλk, and the further
26:1342:59073:17:18:72:448:457:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:away from one is the elasticity of substitutionθkas measured byθk−1.
26:1343:59141:18:18:89:539:439:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Equation (11) is a particular case of equation (10) and so the intuition is identical. The
26:1344:59231:18:18:71:540:421:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:change in the sales share ofidepends on substitution by all producersk.  The extent to
26:1345:59317:18:18:71:539:403:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f7:B:which substitution by producerkmatters depends on how unequallykis exposed toi
26:1346:59395:18:18:71:540:385:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:through its different inputs, on how largekis, and on far away from one is the elasticity of
26:1347:59487:18:18:71:539:367:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:substitution in production ofk. Ifkis small, or is exposed in the same way toithrough all of
26:1348:59579:18:18:71:539:349:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:its inputs, then the extent to which it can substitute amongst its inputs is irrelevant. If the
26:1349:59674:18:18:71:540:331:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:elasticity of substitution ofkis equal to one, then the direct and indirect relative demand
26:1350:59765:18:18:71:539:313:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:expenditure foriarising fromkdoes not change in response to shocks. Equation (11) can
26:1351:59850:18:18:71:539:295:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:be seen as a centrality measure which combines structural microeconomic elasticities of
26:1352:59937:18:18:71:295:277:12:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f5:B:substitution and features of the network.29
26:1353:59980:18:18:89:539:259:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:The Cobb-Douglas case is the knife-edge special case where all the second-order terms
26:1354:60065:18:18:71:539:241:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:are equal to zero and where the first-order approximation is globally accurate. This occurs
26:1355:60156:18:16:82:539:223:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:28There is a connection between these formulas and the gains-from-trade formulas in Arkolakis et al.
26:1356:60256:16:12:72:540:207:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:(2012).    Both  formulas  relate  changes  in  welfare  to  expenditure  shares  and  elasticities  of  substitution.
26:1357:60374:12:12:72:540:195:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:However,  there  are  some  important  differences.    Conceptually,  in  an  open-economy  context,  Hulten’s
26:1358:60484:12:12:72:539:183:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:theorem can no longer be used to capture the effects of shocks on welfare. Because of terms-of-trade effects,
26:1359:60593:12:12:72:540:171:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:the elasticity of welfare with respect to a shock is typicallynotequal to its Domar weight.   However, in
26:1360:60698:12:12:72:540:159:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:Appendix E , we show that the calculation of the gains from trade in a large class of open-economy models is
26:1361:60806:12:12:72:540:147:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:isomorphic to that of the effects of productivity shocks in associated closed-economy models. This mapping
26:1362:60912:12:12:71:539:135:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:allows us to build a formal bridge between our results and theirs, and shows how our results can be used
26:1363:61016:12:12:71:539:123:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:to generalize their formulas to arbitrary networks structures and patterns of microeconomic elasticities of
26:1364:61123:12:8:71:500:111:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:substitution. In ongoing work (Baqaee and Farhi, 2018) we investigate these issues in more detail.
26:1365:61221:8:16:82:539:103:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:29Equation  (11)  is  also  related  to  theconcentrationcentrality  defined  by  Acemoglu  et  al.  (2016),  but
26:1366:61334:16:12:71:539:87:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:generalizes their result by allowing for heterogeneity in the interaction functions, non-symmetric network
26:1367:61440:12:0:71:342:75:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:structures, and micro-founds its use for production networks.
27:1368:61503:0:18:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:because sales shares, and more generally, the whole input-output matrix, are constant and
27:1369:61592:18:18:72:540:690:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:can be taken to be exogenous.  Away from the Cobb-Douglas case, sales shares and the
27:1370:61676:18:18:72:540:672:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:input-output matrix respond endogenously to shocks, and this is precisely what gives rise

30:1570:65743:0:18:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Equation (12) directly expresses the second-order term as a weighted sum of the microeco-

30:1580:66355:18:18:72:539:524:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:is irrelevant whenM=Nis a manifestation of the general principle stated in Proposition
30:1581:66441:18:18:72:539:506:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:7.  WhenM=N, energy is a universal input, and henceVarΩ(0)(Ψ(e))=0.  In this case,
30:1582:66523:18:18:72:540:488:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the household is symmetrically exposed to shocks to energy via the different downstream
30:1583:66610:18:18:72:485:470:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:producers, and so the elasticity of substitution in consumptionθ0is irrelevant.
30:1584:66689:18:18:89:540:452:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:WhenM,Ninsteadθ0matters, with a weight that decreases withN.  Through the
30:1585:66762:18:18:71:540:434:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:lens Proposition 7,VarΩ(0)(Ψ(e))=λ2e(N−M)/N>0 is increasing inM: as heterogeneity in
30:1586:66846:18:18:71:539:416:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:energy-intensity across downstream producers increases, the ability of the household to
30:1587:66933:18:18:71:375:398:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:substitute across these producers matters more and more.
30:1588:66989:18:17:89:540:380:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Becauseθ1<1, whenM=N, the second-order approximation magnifies negative the
30:1589:67064:17:18:71:539:363:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:macroeconomic impact of negative shocks to energy compared to the first-order approxi-
30:1590:67150:18:18:71:540:345:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:mation.  AsMdecreases, this effect becomes weaker, since a lowerMmeans that energy
30:1591:67232:18:18:71:539:327:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:is less of a universal input, and so it becomes easier to substitute away from it further
30:1592:67321:18:18:71:539:309:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:downstream across producers with different energy intensities. The sign of the effect can
30:1593:67410:18:36:71:409:291:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:even flip ifMis low enough and ifθ0is high enough above one.

31:1619:67968:32:18:89:539:610:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:The intuition is that, in a one factor model, we can normalize the wage to one, and then
31:1620:68056:18:18:71:540:592:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:aggregate output depends only on the prices of final goods. A change in the size of theith
31:1621:68146:18:18:72:539:574:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:industry does not affect its price.  Hence, a productivity shock travels downstream from
31:1622:68234:18:18:72:540:556:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:suppliers to their consumers by lowering their marginal costs and hence their prices, but
31:1623:68323:18:18:72:540:538:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:it does not travel upstream from consumers to their suppliers. This result fails whenever
31:1624:68412:18:18:72:540:520:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:there are multiple factors, and by implication when the model does not feature constant
31:1625:68499:18:40:72:167:502:12:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f5:B:returns to scale.34

33:1729:72174:0:18:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:demand expenditure for each factor, and hence the factor income shares, as measured by

34:1848:75883:12:12:72:540:131:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:of (16) would apply where d logΛ/d logAg=δ(g).  This equation establishes that the macro-elasticity of
34:1849:75985:12:12:72:540:119:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:substitution  between  factors  (when  factor  prices  are  exogenous),  is  a  linear  function  of  the  underlying
34:1850:76102:12:12:72:540:107:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:microeconomic elasticities (in fact, a weighted average).  A noteworthy special case of this formula can be
34:1851:76209:12:12:72:540:95:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:applied to Sato (1967) two-level CES production functions which appear frequently in various literatures,

34:1853:76420:12:0:72:98:71:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:2014).

36:1924:78735:36:27:72:264:470:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:Macro-Influence – Multiple Factors
36:1925:78769:27:17:72:540:443:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:In contrast to the case of a single factor, shocks to prices now propagate downstream and
36:1926:78858:17:18:72:540:426:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:upstream. The result derived in Proposition 8 when there is only factor breaks down when
36:1927:78946:18:18:72:540:408:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:there are multiple factors: two producers on which the expenditure by all other producers
36:1928:79035:18:18:72:540:390:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:is the same do not necessarily have the same importance.   This is simply because they
36:1929:79121:18:18:72:540:372:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:might have different direct and indirect exposures to the different factors. As a result, the
36:1930:79214:18:47:72:452:354:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:role of a producer as a consumer matters as well as its role as a supplier.
36:1931:79289:47:31:72:196:307:17:g_d0_f4:17:g_d0_f4:C:5    Beyond CES

37:1995:81705:18:18:71:539:190:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:omy described in Section 2, with arbitrary, and potentially, non-homothetic production
37:1996:81791:18:18:71:539:172:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:functions, an arbitrary number of factors, and arbitrary patterns of input-output linkages.
37:1997:81882:18:18:89:540:154:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Intuitively,Φk(Ψ(i),Ψ(j)) captures the way in whichkredirects demand expenditure
37:1998:81962:18:18:71:539:136:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:towardsiin response to proportional unit decline in the price ofj.  To see this, we make
37:1999:82050:18:17:71:539:118:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:use of the following well-known result (see for example Russell, 2017):  the elasticity of
37:2000:82140:17:18:71:540:101:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the  expenditure  share  of  producerkon  inputxwith  respect  to  the  price  of  inputyis
37:2001:82231:18:0:72:539:83:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:given byδxy+ Ωky(θk(x,y)−1). Equation (18) requires considering, for each pair of inputs
38:2002:82321:0:18:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f5:B:xandy,  how much the proportional reductionΨy jin the price ofyinduced by a unit
38:2003:82401:18:18:72:540:690:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:proportional reduction in the price ofjcauses producerkto increase its expenditure share
38:2004:82489:18:18:72:539:672:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:onx(as measured by−Ωkx[δxy+ Ωky(θk(x,y)−1)]Ψy j) and how muchxis exposed toi(as
38:2005:82568:18:18:72:167:654:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:measured byΨxi).
38:2006:82584:18:18:89:539:636:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Equation  (19)  says  that  this  amounts  to  considering,  for  each  pair  of  inputsxand
38:2007:82676:18:18:72:540:618:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f5:B:y, whether or not increased exposure tojas measured byΨj(x)−Ψj(y), corresponds to
38:2008:82757:18:18:71:539:600:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:increased exposure toias measured byΨi(x)−Ψi(y), and whetherxandyare complements
38:2009:82837:18:18:71:540:582:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:or substitutes as measured by (θk(x,y)−1).  Ifxandyare substitutes, andΨj(x)−Ψj(y)
38:2010:82919:18:18:71:539:564:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:andΨi(x)−Ψi(y) are both positive, then substitution acrossxandybyk, in response to a
38:2011:83003:18:47:72:384:546:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:shock to a decrease in the price ofj, increases demand fori.
38:2012:83063:47:30:72:290:499:17:g_d0_f4:17:g_d0_f4:C:6    Quantitative Illustration
38:2013:83093:30:18:72:540:469:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:In this section,  we develop some illustrative quantitative applications of our results to
38:2014:83183:18:18:72:540:451:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:gauge the practical importance of the nonlinearities that we have identified. We perform
38:2015:83271:18:18:72:540:433:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:three  exercises  focusing  on  macroeconmic  phenomena  at  different  frequencies.    First,
38:2016:83365:18:18:72:540:415:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:we calibrate a multi-sector business-cycle model with sectoral productivity shocks.  We
38:2017:83452:18:18:72:540:397:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:match the observed input-output data, we use the best available information to choose
38:2018:83537:18:18:72:540:379:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the structural (micro) elasticities of substitution, and we match the volatility of sectoral
38:2019:83629:18:18:72:540:361:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:shocks at business cycle horizons. We compare the outcome of the nonlinear model to its
38:2020:83716:18:18:72:540:343:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:first-order approximation.  In the second exercise, we study the macroeconomic impact
38:2021:83801:18:18:72:540:325:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:of the energy crisis of the 1970s using a non-parametric generalization of Hulten (1978)
38:2022:83889:18:18:72:540:307:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:that takes second-order terms into account. In the third and final exercise, we investigate
38:2023:83980:18:18:72:540:289:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the importance of nonlinearities inherent in Baumol’s cost disease for long-run aggregate
38:2024:84069:18:40:72:463:271:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:TFP growth. All our exercises suggest that production is highly nonlinear.
38:2025:84143:40:22:72:540:231:14:g_d0_f4:14:g_d0_f4:C:6.1    A  Quantitative  Multi-Sector  Business-Cycle  Model  with  Sectoral

39:2113:85752:29:16:82:539:199:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:37For comparison, Table 3 in Appendix C shows the macro-moments for the model using the second-
39:2114:85847:16:12:72:540:183:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:order approximation.  The second-order approximation does a very good job at capturing the mean and
39:2115:85946:12:12:72:540:171:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:standard deviation of aggregate output at both annual and quadrennial frequencies. It also performs well for
39:2116:86054:12:12:72:540:159:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:skewness and kurtosis at an annual frequency, but less so at a quadrennial frequency. Basically, the quality
39:2117:86162:12:12:72:540:147:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:of the approximation is worse for larger shocks and higher moments of output.  Of course, whenever it is
39:2118:86266:12:12:72:540:135:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:feasible to solve the model non-linearly, the fully nonlinear solution is preferable.  However, our (pen and
39:2119:86374:12:11:72:540:123:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:paper) approach also sheds light on the mechanisms driving nonlinearities that would be lost were we to
39:2120:86477:11:12:72:539:112:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:simply solve a series of nonlinear equations on a computer. Furthermore, our sufficient statistics approach
39:2121:86584:12:0:72:540:100:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:allows us to construct the second-order approximation without needing to fully specify the nonlinear model.
40:2122:86693:0:18:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:whereXiare units of goodipurchased andˆXiare the units of goodiactually used. When
40:2123:86775:18:36:72:262:690:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f5:B:κ=0, there are no adjustment costs.
40:2124:86810:36:27:72:187:654:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:Data and Calibration
40:2125:86830:27:18:72:540:627:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:We work with the 88 sector US KLEMS annual input-output data from Dale Jorgenson and
40:2126:86914:18:18:72:540:609:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:his collaborators, dropping the government sectors. The dataset contains sectoral output
40:2127:87002:18:18:72:540:591:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:and inputs from 1960 to 2005.  We use the sector-level TFP series computed by Carvalho
40:2128:87088:18:17:72:428:573:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:and Gabaix (2013) using the methodology of Jorgenson et al. (1987).
40:2129:87155:17:18:89:539:556:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:We calibrate the expenditure share parameters to match the input-output table, using
40:2130:87239:18:18:72:540:538:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:1982  (the  middle  of  the  sample)  as  the  base  year.    We  set  sectoral  TFP  shocks  to  be
40:2131:87339:18:18:72:539:520:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:lognormally distributed so that logAi∼ N(−Σii/2,Σii), whereΣiiis the sample variance
40:2132:87423:18:18:72:539:502:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:of log TFP growth for industryi.  We work with uncorrelated sectoral shocks since the
40:2133:87508:18:18:72:540:484:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:average correlation between sectoral growth rates is small (less than 5%).   Our results
40:2134:87596:18:18:72:539:466:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:are not significantly affected if we matched the whole covariance matrix of sectoral TFP
40:2135:87684:18:18:72:113:448:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:instead.
40:2136:87692:18:18:89:539:430:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:We consider shocks at annual and quadrennial horizon,  the latter corresponding to
40:2137:87774:18:18:72:540:412:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the average period of a business cycle.  The average standard deviation at a quadrennial
40:2138:87862:18:18:72:540:394:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:frequency is about twice its value at an annual frequency. In fact, this is the only difference
40:2139:87957:18:18:72:540:376:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:between the annual and quadriennal calibrations.  Nonlinearities, which matter more for
40:2140:88044:18:18:72:540:358:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:bigger shocks, are more important at a quadriennal frequency than at an annual frequency.
40:2141:88133:18:18:89:539:340:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Our specification assumes only three distinct structural microeconomic elasticities of
40:2142:88219:18:17:72:540:322:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:substitution. This is because estimates of more disaggregated elasticities are not available.
40:2143:88312:17:18:72:539:305:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:For our benchmark calibration, we set (σ,θ,ε)=(0.9,0.5,0.001).  We set the elasticity of
40:2144:88400:18:18:72:539:287:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:substitution in consumptionσ=0.9, following Atalay (2017), Herrendorf et al. (2013), and
40:2145:88488:18:18:71:539:269:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Oberfield and Raval (2014), all of whom use an elasticity of substitution in consumption
40:2146:88576:18:18:71:539:251:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:(across industries) of slightly less than one. For the elasticity of substitution across value-
40:2147:88671:18:18:71:539:233:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:added and intermediate inputs, we setθ=0.5. This accords with the estimates of Atalay
40:2148:88756:18:18:72:539:215:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:(2017), who estimates this parameter to be between 0.4 and 0.8, as well as Boehm et al.
40:2149:88843:18:18:72:540:197:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:(2017),  who estimate this elasticity to be close to zero.   Finally,  we set the elasticity of
40:2150:88938:18:18:72:539:179:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:substitution across intermediate inputs to beε=0.001, which matches the estimates of
40:2151:89022:18:18:72:145:161:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Atalay (2017).
40:2152:89036:18:18:89:540:143:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Owing to uncertainty surrounding the estimates for (σ,θ,ε), we include many robust-
40:2153:89119:18:18:72:540:125:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:ness checks in Tables 4-7 in Appendix C. In the main text in Tables 1 and 2, we focus on
40:2154:89207:18:18:72:540:107:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:four sets of elasticities (σ,θ,ε):  our benchmark calibration (0.9,0.5,0.001);  a calibration
40:2155:89300:18:18:72:540:89:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:with lower but still plausible elasticities (0.7,0.3,0.001); a calibration with higher elastici-
40:2156:89396:18:0:72:540:71:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:ties (0.9,0.6,0.2); and a (close to) Cobb-Douglas calibration (0.99,0.99,0.99).  In Appendix
41:2157:89490:0:18:72:539:708:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:C,  we  report  robstness  checks  for  different  values  of  these  elasticities  on  a  grid  with
41:2158:89591:18:18:72:539:690:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f5:B:σ∈ {0.8,0.9,0.99},θ∈ {0.4,0.5,0.6,0.99},andε∈ {0.001,0.2,0.99}.  Our results in Table 1
41:2159:89678:18:18:72:539:672:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:are not sensitive to the exact value of (σ,θ,ε) provided that the elasticities are collectively
41:2160:89773:18:18:72:527:654:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:low enough that the calibration matches the observed volatility of the Domar weights.
41:2161:89858:18:18:89:539:636:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Since the volatility of Domar weights are a measure of the size of the second-order
41:2162:89941:18:18:72:540:618:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:terms in the model, we use the volatility of Domar weights as a sanity check for our cali-
41:2163:90031:18:0:72:258:600:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f6:B:bration. Specifically, we targetσλ=
41:2164:90066:0:12:261:271:609:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:C:∑

41:2168:90289:18:18:71:540:546:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f5:B:σλ≈0.27.   With  no  labor-reallocation  and  no  adjustment  costs,  our  baseline  calibra-
41:2169:90382:18:18:71:539:528:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:tions match these numbers relatively well; the lower-elasticity calibrations overshoot; the
41:2170:90473:18:18:71:539:510:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:higher-elasticity calibrations undershoot; and the Cobb-Douglas calibrations deliver zero
41:2171:90562:18:18:71:539:492:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:volatility of the Domar weights. Allowing for labor re-allocation reduces the volatility of
41:2172:90653:18:36:71:428:474:12:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f5:B:the Domar weights, and introducing adjustment costs increases it.38
41:2173:90720:36:26:71:260:438:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:Results with No Adjustment Costs
41:2174:90752:26:18:71:539:412:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:We start by setting adjustment costs to zero.  Table 1 displays the mean, standard devi-
41:2175:90840:18:18:71:539:394:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:ation, skewness, and excess kurtosis of log aggregate output for various specifications.
41:2176:90928:18:18:71:539:376:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:For comparison,  the table also shows these moments for aggregate TFP growth in the
41:2177:91011:18:18:71:540:358:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:data.39In addition, we also report the volatility of the Domar weights, both in the model

41:2179:91188:18:18:71:539:322:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:vations of aggregate TFP, we do not report the skewness and excess kurtosis (the implied
41:2180:91276:18:17:71:539:304:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:confidence intervals for these estimates would be so large as to make the point estimates

41:2182:91449:18:18:71:306:269:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the elasticities of substitution for robustness.
41:2183:91497:18:18:89:539:251:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Overall,  the  model  with  full  reallocation  is  unable  to  replicate  the  volatility  of  the

41:2187:91857:19:16:82:539:178:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:38To match the data, we assume that changes in sectoral TFPs are the sole driver of fluctuations in the
41:2188:91960:16:12:72:540:162:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:Domar weight.  Other types of shocks, besides industry-level TFP shocks, could also drive volatility to the
41:2189:92067:12:12:72:540:150:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:Domar weights (for example shocks to the composition of demand).   While such shocks, whatever they
41:2190:92166:12:11:72:540:138:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:are, would also indicate the presence nonlinearities, they would imply different elasticities of substitution
41:2191:92275:11:12:72:540:127:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:for the calibration of the micro-elasticities of substitution.   We abstract from this issue in calibrating the
41:2192:92386:12:9:72:243:115:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:parameters of the model in Section 6.1.
41:2193:92425:9:15:82:539:106:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:39Since our model has inelastic factor supply, its output is more comparable to aggregate TFP than to real
41:2194:92531:15:12:72:540:91:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:GDP. As shown by Gabaix (2011) and Carvalho and Gabaix (2013), elastic capital and labor supply would

42:2219:93660:40:14:72:540:161:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Table 1:  Simulated and estimated moments.  For the data, we use the demeaned growth
42:2220:93744:14:15:72:540:147:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:rate of aggregate TFP. For the model,  we use the sample moments of log output.   The
42:2221:93829:15:14:72:540:132:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:simulated moments are calculated from 50,000 draws. Skewness and kurtosis of the data
42:2222:93914:14:0:72:493:118:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:are impossible to estimate with enough precision and so we do not report them.
43:2223:93994:0:18:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:model without reallocation is able to match the volatility of the Domar weights, which is
43:2224:94083:18:18:72:287:690:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:consistent with the intuition of Section 3.
43:2225:94126:18:18:89:539:672:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Let  us  consider  each  moment  in  turn  starting  with  the  mean.   For  our  benchmark
43:2226:94217:18:18:72:539:654:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:calibration (σ,θ,ε)=(0.9,0.5,0.001), the model without reallocation can match the volatil-
43:2227:94307:18:18:71:539:636:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:ity of Domar weights at both annual and quadrennial frequency.  The reductions in the
43:2228:94392:18:18:71:540:618:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:mean are around 0.3% at annual and just under 2% at quadrennial frequency.  Since our
43:2229:94477:18:18:71:539:600:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:lognormal shocks are calibrated to have a mean of 1 in levels, as we increase the variance,
43:2230:94568:18:18:71:539:582:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the mean of the log declines.   We can net out this mechanical effect by subtracting the
43:2231:94656:18:18:71:539:564:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:average loss in performance from the ones in the loglinear Cobb-Douglas model.  So, for
43:2232:94743:18:18:71:540:546:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:example, at the annual frequency, this would result in a loss of 0.34%−0.011%=0.23%,
43:2233:94827:18:18:71:539:528:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:and at quadrennial frequency, the loss is 1.87%−0.57%=1.30%.  These numbers, which
43:2234:94909:18:18:71:539:510:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:identify the welfare costs of sectoral shocks arising from concavity in production, can be
43:2235:94999:18:18:71:539:492:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:compared with the welfare costs of fluctuations`a la Lucas (1987) arising from concavity
43:2236:95087:18:17:71:484:474:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:in utility, which are around 0.01% and 0.05% respectively in these calibrations.
43:2237:95167:17:18:89:539:457:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:The  losses  increase  as  we  pump  up  the  degree  of  nonlinearity,  and  fall  to  roughly
43:2238:95262:18:18:71:539:439:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:0.1% and 0.6% for an approximately Cobb-Douglas model. The reason why the reduction
43:2239:95345:18:18:71:539:421:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:in the mean for the loglinear Cobb-Douglas model is nonzero is that we normalize the
43:2240:95429:18:18:71:539:403:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:shocks to have a mean of 1 in levels (and hence a negative mean in logs). A qualitatively
43:2241:95518:18:18:71:539:385:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:similar pattern holds for the model with full reallocation.   In that case,  the reductions
43:2242:95609:18:18:71:540:367:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:in  the  mean  are  smaller  0.2%−0.1%=0.1%  at  annual  and  1.1%−0.57%=0.46%  at
43:2243:95691:18:18:72:540:349:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:quadrennial frequency. Unsurprisingly, the approximately Cobb-Douglas model behaves
43:2244:95774:18:18:72:540:331:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:similarly regardless of the mobility of labor — this follows from the fact that Hulten’s
43:2245:95862:18:18:72:540:313:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:theorem holds globally for a Cobb-Douglas model where no labor reallocation takes place
43:2246:95949:18:18:72:300:295:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:in equilibrium whether or not it is allowed.
43:2247:95993:18:18:89:539:277:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:At an annual frequency,  both models undershoot a little on the overall volatility of
43:2248:96078:18:18:72:540:259:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:aggregate TFP somewhat. One reason why the model undershoots on standard deviation,
43:2249:96161:18:17:72:540:241:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:particularly at annual frequency, is that we restrict the industry-level productivity shocks
43:2250:96253:17:18:72:540:224:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:to be independent, whereas in the data, particularly at higher frequencies, they feature
43:2251:96341:18:18:72:540:206:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:some correlation.   At a quadrennial frequency,  the model better matches the volatility
43:2252:96429:18:18:72:540:188:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:of aggregate TFP. The degree of nonlinearity makes little difference for the volatlity of
43:2253:96518:18:18:72:540:170:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:aggregate TFP at an annual frequency.40Nonlinearities matter more for the volatility of
43:2254:96605:18:19:72:451:152:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:aggregate TFP at a quadrennial frequency because the shocks are larger.
43:2255:96676:19:16:82:539:133:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:40Whereas for the mean, skewness, and kurtosis, the second-order terms are the dominant power in the
43:2256:96776:16:12:72:540:117:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:Taylor expansion (since the linear terms have no effect), for the variance, the dominant power is the linear
43:2257:96884:12:12:72:540:105:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:term.  For example, lettingσbe the standard deviation of the shocks, the approximation of the variance in
43:2258:96989:12:12:72:539:93:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:Appendix D shows that the contribution of the linear terms scales inσ2, whereas that of the nonlinear terms
43:2259:97096:12:0:72:122:81:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:scales inσ4.
44:2260:97110:0:18:89:539:708:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Finally, the models (with and without reallocation) generate negative skewness and
44:2261:97192:18:18:72:540:690:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:some positive excessive kurtosis (in fact, a very high amount for the quadrennial specifi-
44:2262:97282:18:18:72:540:672:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:cations without reallocation).  The skewness and excess kurtosis fatten the left tail of the
44:2263:97374:18:18:72:540:654:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:distribution, providing an endogenous explanation for “rare disasters”. Unlike Acemoglu
44:2264:97461:18:18:72:540:636:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:et al. (2017) or Barro (2006), to achieve rare disasters, we do not need to assume fat-tailed
44:2265:97554:18:18:72:540:618:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:exogenous shocks nor rule out “rare bonanzas” a priori.  Instead these features are en-
44:2266:97641:18:18:72:540:600:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:dogenously generated by the nonlinearities in the model.  This can be seen in Figure 5,
44:2267:97728:18:18:72:540:582:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:where we plot the histograms for the benchmark calibrations with no reallocation (which
44:2268:97815:18:18:72:540:564:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:match the volatility of Domar weights) and for a loglinear approximation subject to the
44:2269:97902:18:18:72:540:546:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:same shocks.  As expected, nonlinearities are more important at a quadrennial frequency
44:2270:97989:18:183:72:459:528:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:than at an annual frequency because the shocks are larger (more volatile).
